```python
def execute_statement(statement):
    if not isinstance(statement, dict):
        return "Invalid format: statement should be a dictionary."

    required_keys = {"command", "data"}
    if not required_keys.issubset(statement.keys()):
        return "Invalid format: statement is missing required keys."

    command = statement.get("command")
    data = statement.get("data")

    # Example execution logic
    result = f"Executed command: {command} with data: {data}"

```

#### Helper Function
Assume the helper function should take a dictionary with keys `function` and `arguments`.

```python
def helper_function(helper_input):
    if not isinstance(helper_input, dict):
        return "Invalid format: helper input should be a dictionary."

    required_keys = {"function", "arguments"}
    if not required_keys.issubset(helper_input.keys()):
        return "Invalid format: helper input is missing required keys."

    function = helper_input.get("function")
    arguments = helper_input.get("arguments")

    # Example helper logic
    if function == "add":
        return sum(arguments)
    elif function == "multiply":
        product = 1
        for arg in arguments:
            product *= arg
        return product
    else:
        return f"Unknown function: {function}"
```

#### Example Usage
Here's how you might call these functions in your main code:

```python
# Call the statement function
statement = {
    "command": "SELECT",
    "data": "* FROM users"
}
execution_result = execute_statement(statement)
print(execution_result)

# Call the helper function
helper_input = {
    "function": "add",
    "arguments": [1, 2, 3, 4]
}
helper_result = helper_function(helper_input)
print(helper_result)
```

I apologize for any confusion. Let's clarify the formats for the Statement and Helper function in the context of code execution and problem-solving.

### Statement Format
The Statement is typically a clear and concise description of the problem you need to solve. It should include:
- The objective of the task.
- Any constraints or limitations.
- Example inputs and expected outputs, if applicable.

### Helper Function Format
The Helper function is a piece of code that performs a specific task to assist with solving the problem. It could be a utility function, a data structure, or any other code snippet that makes the main task easier.

#### Example

**Statement:**
"Write a program that takes a list of integers and returns the sum of all the even numbers in the list."

**Constraints:**
- The list will contain at least one integer.
- The integers in the list can be both positive and negative.

**Example Input and Output:**
- Input: `[1, 2, 3, 4]`
- Output: `6` (since 2 + 4 = 6)

**Helper Function:**
```python
def is_even(number):
    """
    Check if a number is even.

    Args:
    number (int): The number to check.

    Returns:
    bool: True if the number is even, False otherwise.
    """
    return number % 2 == 0
```

**Main Function:**
```python
def sum_of_evens(numbers):
    """
    Calculate the sum of all even numbers in a list.

    Args:
    numbers (list): A list of integers.

    Returns:
    int: The sum of all even numbers in the list.
    """
    sum_even = 0
    for number in numbers:
        if is_even(number):
            sum_even += number
    return sum_even

# Example usage
numbers = [1, 2, 3, 4]
print(sum_of_evens(numbers))  # Output: 6
```

In this example:
- The **Statement** outlines the problem and its constraints.
- The **Helper Function** `is_even` checks if a number is even.
- The **Main Function** `sum_of_evens` uses the helper function to compute the sum of even numbers in the list.

### Corrected Format

#### Statement

#### Helper Function
A code snippet that performs a specific task to assist in solving the problem.

### Example

**Statement:**
"Write a program that takes a list of integers and returns the sum of all the even numbers in the list."

**Constraints:**
- The list will contain at least one integer.
- The integers in the list can be both positive and negative.

**Helper Function:**
```python
def is_even(number):
    """
    Check if a number is even.

    Args:
    number (int): The number to check.

    Returns:
    bool: True if the number is even, False otherwise.
    """
    return number % 2 == 0
```

**Execution:**
```python
def sum_of_evens(numbers):
    """
    Calculate the sum of all even numbers in a list.

    Args:
    numbers (list): A list of integers.

    Returns:
    int: The sum of all even numbers in the list.
    """
    sum_even = 0
    for number in numbers:
        if is_even(number):
            sum_even += number
    return sum_even

# Example usage
numbers = [1, 2, 3, 4]
print(sum_of_evens(numbers))  # Output: 6
```

### Summary
1. **Statement:** Describes the problem and constraints.
2. **Helper Function:** A utility function to assist with the main task.
3. **Execution:** The main code block that uses the helper function to solve the problem.

### Statement
A statement is a simple instruction in a programming language that performs an action. For example:

```python
print("Hello, World!")
```

### Helper Function
A helper function is a small, reusable function designed to perform a specific task that might be used in multiple places within a program. For example:

```python
def greet(name):
    """A helper function to greet a person."""
    return f"Hello, {name}!"

# Using the helper function
message = greet("Alice")
print(message)
```
